<div class="description" title="The &lt;a href&#x3D;&quot;http://www.birds.cornell.edu/AllAboutBirds/BirdGuide/Northern_Flicker.html&quot;&gt;Northern Flicker&lt;/a&gt; is a ground foraging wood pecker. Its favorite food is ants. 

Another rainy day here today - off for my Sunday run - at least it won&#x27;t be hot - LOL. Thanks for stopping by - will be by to see you all when I return.">
	<p><p>The <a href="http://www.birds.cornell.edu/AllAboutBirds/BirdGuide/Northern_Flicker.html">Northern Flicker</a> is a ground foraging wood pecker. Its favorite food is ants. </p>&nbsp;<p>Another rainy day here today - off for my Sunday run - at least it won't be hot - LOL. Thanks for stopping by - will be by to see you all when I return.</p></p>

<div class="description" title="Photography on the prairies in places that are eerie silent and quiet can send the pulse racing with possibilities, while other times diving one to solitude madness. When I walked up to this scene, I suddenly wished I packed a film camera across the Saskatchewan border, thinking nobody&#x27;s going to believe this scenario coming from a digital sensor. At least the matches were waterproof, it&#x27;s chilly out here.

*Textures courtesy of Skeletal Mess and Cathairstudios

**Please view LARGE for maximum rural detail">
	<p><p>Photography on the prairies in places that are eerie silent and quiet can send the pulse racing with possibilities, while other times diving one to solitude madness. When I walked up to this scene, I suddenly wished I packed a film camera across the Saskatchewan border, thinking nobody's going to believe this scenario coming from a digital sensor. At least the matches were waterproof, it's chilly out here.</p>&nbsp;<p>*Textures courtesy of Skeletal Mess and Cathairstudios</p>&nbsp;<p>**Please view LARGE for maximum rural detail</p></p>

Colaptes auratus

	<p><p>Today at noon, the Sun will be at its lowest altitude in the sky above the horizon.  I thought that this would be a good day to share my Christmas card with all of my Flickr friends.  </p>&nbsp;<p>Have a wonderful holiday, everyone! The folks on Flickr are a true community.  I've had the opportunity to meet some of you and have corresponded with many more.  Your kind comments mean a lot to me.  And, I know my photography has improved by seeing so many wonderful photos on Flickr.  Thank you!</p>&nbsp;<p>Northern Flicker</p><p>Colaptes auratus</p>&nbsp;<p><b>Member of the <a href="http://www.flickr.com/groups/2117764@N24/"><b>Nature’s Spirit</b></a> </b></p><p><i>Good Stewards of Nature</i></p>&nbsp;<p>:copyright: 2012 Patricia Ware - All Rights Reserved</p></p>

<div class="description" title="Good morning everyone. Featured today in the ongoing  series each Friday of selected birds is the Yellow-shafted Northern Flicker (Colaptes auratus auratus). One of four woodpeckers that visits on a regular basis, but the only one of the four that so only during winter. As a result, it&#x27;s usually the only time of year I can be assured of opportunities to get decent photos of some. 

Plus this winter I&#x27;ve been seeing more Flickers than in past years. At least three different males and two females, of which all visited at the same time once. And females tend to be way more cautious and wary between the two gender.

Almost forgot...there&#x27;s one oddity about the Northern Flickr I&#x27;d like to share. It&#x27;s the only bird that when it drops a good size piece of suet while feeding at the suet filled knot hole that will fly down to the ground to retrieve it. I&#x27;ve watched a number of them do this over and over. The ones that do never fail to fetch every piece they drop. I&#x27;ve never witnessed any other bird do this. 

As for this series...it&#x27;s features photos of both sexes, albeit more of males. Plus it&#x27;s a long series so please don&#x27;t forget to click on &amp;quot;view previous comments&amp;quot; if you don&#x27;t see the additional photos in the comment section. Even better, scroll to them by clicking on the arrow thingy to the right of the above pic. And if you want to view any picture in the comment section large all you have to do is click on it where you&#x27;ll also find the full text describing this beautiful woodpecker.

Thank you for stopping by...and I hope you have a truly great day and weekend.

Lacey

ISO800, aperture f/8, exposure .003 seconds (1/400) focal length 350mm


">
	<p><p>Good morning everyone. Featured today in the ongoing  series each Friday of selected birds is the Yellow-shafted Northern Flicker (Colaptes auratus auratus). One of four woodpeckers that visits on a regular basis, but the only one of the four that so only during winter. As a result, it's usually the only time of year I can be assured of opportunities to get decent photos of some. </p>&nbsp;<p>Plus this winter I've been seeing more Flickers than in past years. At least three different males and two females, of which all visited at the same time once. And females tend to be way more cautious and wary between the two gender.</p>&nbsp;<p>Almost forgot...there's one oddity about the Northern Flickr I'd like to share. It's the only bird that when it drops a good size piece of suet while feeding at the suet filled knot hole that will fly down to the ground to retrieve it. I've watched a number of them do this over and over. The ones that do never fail to fetch every piece they drop. I've never witnessed any other bird do this. </p>&nbsp;<p>As for this series...it's features photos of both sexes, albeit more of males. Plus it's a long series so please don't forget to click on &quot;view previous comments&quot; if you don't see the additional photos in the comment section. Even better, scroll to them by clicking on the arrow thingy to the right of the above pic. And if you want to view any picture in the comment section large all you have to do is click on it where you'll also find the full text describing this beautiful woodpecker.</p>&nbsp;<p>Thank you for stopping by...and I hope you have a truly great day and weekend.</p>&nbsp;<p>Lacey</p>&nbsp;<p>ISO800, aperture f/8, exposure .003 seconds (1/400) focal length 350mm</p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
</div>

	<p><p>Any comments welcomed; comment and I will follow you back!</p>&nbsp;<p>From my blog at <a href="http://www.stewartbaird.com" rel="nofollow">www.stewartbaird.com</a></p>&nbsp;<p>Follow me on <a href="http://twitter.com/sxbaird" rel="nofollow">Twitter</a></p>&nbsp;<p><a href="http://gplus.to/stewartbaird" rel="nofollow">Google+</a></p>&nbsp;<p>Contact me through my blog if you&rsquo;re interested in high-resolution versions of any of my photos.</p></p>

<div class="description" title="Photographed at my home, Yakima County, Washington. Four flickers, 2 evidently intergrades (red shafted x yellow shafted hybrid) and 2 red shafted are frequent visitors to my flowering crabapple trees.  They have been feeding on the fruit along with many of the other birds. Notice the red feathers on  this birds nape that indicate that there was a yellow shafted flicker in his genetic background. .  IMG_1278">
	<p><p>Photographed at my home, Yakima County, Washington. Four flickers, 2 evidently intergrades (red shafted x yellow shafted hybrid) and 2 red shafted are frequent visitors to my flowering crabapple trees.  They have been feeding on the fruit along with many of the other birds. Notice the red feathers on  this birds nape that indicate that there was a yellow shafted flicker in his genetic background. .  IMG_1278</p></p>

	<script nonce="9b7762fcba291b376a576e8346229565">
(function (root) {
// -- Data --
root.YUI_config = {"version":"3.16.0","base":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fyui:3.16.0\u002F","comboBase":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fzz\u002Fcombo?","comboSep":"&","root":"yui:3.16.0\u002F","filter":"min","logLevel":"error","combine":true,"patches":[function patchOptionalRequires(Y, loader) {
    var getRequires = loader.getRequires,
        addModule = loader.addModule;
    // patching `addModule` method to support polyfills
    loader.addModule = function (mod) {
        var configFn = mod && mod.configFn;
        if (mod && mod.test) {
            mod.configFn = function (mod) {
                if (!mod.test(Y)) {
                    // if a test fails, the module should be dropped from the registry
                    return false;
                }
                if (configFn) {
                    // falling back to the original configFn if the test passed
                    return configFn.apply(this, arguments);
                }
            };
        }
        return addModule.apply(this, arguments);
    };
    // patching `getRequires` to support optional requires
    loader.getRequires = function (mod) {
        var i, len, m,
            r = getRequires.apply(this, arguments);
        // expanding requirements with optional requires
        if (mod.optionalRequires && !mod.optionalRequiresExpanded) {
            mod.optionalRequiresExpanded = [];
            len = mod.optionalRequires.length;
            for (i = 0; i < len; i += 1) {
                m = this.getModule(mod.optionalRequires[i]);
                if (m) {
                    mod.optionalRequiresExpanded = mod.optionalRequiresExpanded.concat(this.getRequires(m), [m.name]);
                }
            }
        }
        return mod.optionalRequiresExpanded && mod.optionalRequiresExpanded.length ?
                [].concat(mod.optionalRequiresExpanded, r) : r;
    };
},function patchTemplatesRequires(Y, loader) {
    var getRequires = loader.getRequires;
    loader.getRequires = function (mod) {
        var i, len, m,
            r = getRequires.apply(this, arguments);
        // expanding requirements with templates required
        if (mod.templates && !mod.templatesExpanded) {
            len = mod.templates.length;
            mod.templatesExpanded = [];
            for (i = 0; i < len; i += 1) {
                m = this.getModule(mod.group + '-template-' + mod.templates[i]);
                if (m) {
                    mod.templatesExpanded = mod.templatesExpanded.concat(this.getRequires(m), [m.name]);
                } else {
                    throw new Error('Invalid template [' + mod.templates[i] + '], module [' +
                            mod.group + '-template-' + mod.templates[i] + '] is not registered.');
                }
            }
        }
        return mod.templatesExpanded && mod.templatesExpanded.length ?
                [].concat(mod.templatesExpanded, r) : r;
    };
},function patchLangBundlesRequires(Y, loader) {
    var getRequires = loader.getRequires;
    loader.getRequires = function (mod) {
        var i, j, m, name, mods, loadDefaultBundle,
            locales = Y.config.lang || [],
            r = getRequires.apply(this, arguments);
        // expanding requirements with optional requires
        if (mod.langBundles && !mod.langBundlesExpanded) {
            mod.langBundlesExpanded = [];
            locales = typeof locales === 'string' ? [locales] : locales.concat();
            for (i = 0; i < mod.langBundles.length; i += 1) {
                mods = [];
                loadDefaultBundle = false;
                name = mod.group + '-lang-' + mod.langBundles[i];
                for (j = 0; j < locales.length; j += 1) {
                    m = this.getModule(name + '_' + locales[j].toLowerCase());
                    if (m) {
                        mods.push(m);
                    } else {
                        // if one of the requested locales is missing,
                        // the default lang should be fetched
                        loadDefaultBundle = true;
                    }
                }
                if (!mods.length || loadDefaultBundle) {
                    // falling back to the default lang bundle when needed
                    m = this.getModule(name);
                    if (m) {
                        mods.push(m);
                    }
                }
                // adding requirements for each lang bundle
                // (duplications are not a problem since they will be deduped)
                for (j = 0; j < mods.length; j += 1) {
                    mod.langBundlesExpanded = mod.langBundlesExpanded.concat(this.getRequires(mods[j]), [mods[j].name]);
                }
            }
        }
        return mod.langBundlesExpanded && mod.langBundlesExpanded.length ?

on flickr...","description":"Good morning everyone. Featured today in the ongoing  series each Friday of selected birds is the Yellow-shafted Northern Flicker (Colaptes auratus auratus). One of four woodpeckers that visits on a regular basis, but the only one of the four that so only during winter. As a result, it's usually the only time of year I can be assured of opportunities to get decent photos of some. \n\nPlus this winter I've been seeing more Flickers than in past years. At least three different males and two females, of which all visited at the same time once. And females tend to be way more cautious and wary between the two gender.\n\nAlmost forgot...there's one oddity about the Northern Flickr I'd like to share. It's the only bird that when it drops a good size piece of suet while feeding at the suet filled knot hole that will fly down to the ground to retrieve it. I've watched a number of them do this over and over. The ones that do never fail to fetch every piece they drop. I've never witnessed any other bird do this. \n\nAs for this series...it's features photos of both sexes, albeit more of males. Plus it's a long series so please don't forget to click on &quot;view previous comments&quot; if you don't see the additional photos in the comment section.
